## OpenHands Workspace Rules

- The provided working directory is the only submission surface for this evaluation.
- Do not `git clone`, `git init`, or fetch the target repository into the working directory or any of its subdirectories.
- Use MCP to inspect remote code, then create or edit only the files you need directly in the working directory using repository-relative paths.
- The verifier only reads changes from the provided working directory, not from any self-cloned checkout.


# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--v11.4.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana--v11.4.0$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Onboarding: Grafana Codebase Orientation

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/grafana--v11.4.0 (mirror of grafana/grafana)
**Task Type:** Codebase Orientation (analysis only — no code changes)

## Scenario

You are a new platform engineer joining the Grafana team. Your first task is to understand the codebase architecture — how the Go backend, React frontend, plugin system, and provisioning pipeline fit together. The codebase is large (~1.4GB, mixed Go/TypeScript/React), so targeted exploration is essential.

## Your Task

Explore the Grafana codebase and answer the following questions. Write your answers to `/logs/agent/onboarding.md`.

### 1. Main Entry Points
Where is the main server binary entry point? What CLI framework does Grafana use? How does the server bootstrap (what services/registries are initialized at startup)?

### 2. Core Backend Packages
Name at least 5 key Go packages under `pkg/` and describe their responsibilities. Include: API routing, service registry, data source proxy, alerting, and authentication.

### 3. Datasource Plugin Architecture
How does Grafana's plugin system work? Where are built-in datasource plugins defined? How does the backend communicate with plugin processes (gRPC, HTTP)? What is the role of the `grafana-plugin-sdk-go`?

### 4. Dashboard Provisioning Pipeline
Trace how a dashboard defined in a YAML provisioning file gets loaded into Grafana. What is the provisioning service? Where are provisioning configs read from? How do they get persisted to the database?

### 5. Frontend Build System
What frontend framework and build tools does Grafana use? How is the React frontend organized (packages, workspace structure)? Where is the main frontend entry point?

### 6. Extension: Adding a New Panel Plugin
If you needed to add a new visualization panel plugin, what steps would be needed? Which directories and configuration files would you touch? How does the plugin registry discover new panels?

## Output Requirements

Write a markdown document to `/logs/agent/onboarding.md` with numbered sections (1-6) matching the questions above. For each section:
- Be specific: include file paths, package names, function names
- Cite the actual code — reference specific files you explored
- Keep each section focused (2-4 paragraphs)

## Constraints

- Do NOT modify any source files
- Exploration and documentation only
- Be specific — include file paths, package names, function names

COMPLETED:
- Task 1: Explored main entry points
  - Primary binary: `pkg/cmd/grafana/main.go` — uses `github.com/urfave/cli/v2`, calls `MainApp()` which builds a `*cli.App` with `ServerCommand` and `CLICommand` subcommands
  - Legacy binary: `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/main.go` — thin wrapper calling `cmd.RunGrafanaCmd("server")`

It covers the six areas you need to understand before making your first meaningful contribution: server bootstrap, core backend packages, datasource plugin architecture, dashboard provisioning, the frontend build system, and how to add a new panel plugin.\n\n---\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Repository Layout](#1-repository-layout)\n2. [Main Entry Points and Server Bootstrap](#2-main-entry-points-and-server-bootstrap)\n3. [Core Backend Packages](#3-core-backend-packages)\n4. [Adding a New Panel Plugin](#7-adding-a-new-panel-plugin)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Repository Layout\n\n```\ngrafana/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 pkg/                        # All Go backend code\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 cmd/grafana/            # Primary CLI entry point\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 cmd/grafana-server/     # Feature-area modules (dashboards, explore, \u2026)\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 plugins/\n\u2502   \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 panel/          # Built-in panel plugins (timeseries, table, \u2026)\n\u2502   \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 datasource/     # Built-in datasource frontend plugins\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 sass/                   # Global SCSS themes\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 packages/                   # Published npm packages (@grafana/data, ui, runtime, \u2026)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 plugins-bundled/            # Bundled (non-core) plugins\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 scripts/webpack/            # Webpack configuration\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 e2e/                        # End-to-end test suites (Cypress + Playwright)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Main Entry Points and Server Bootstrap\n\n### 2.1 Binary Entry Points\n\n**Primary binary** \u2014 `pkg/cmd/grafana/main.go`\n\n```\nmain()\n  \u2514\u2500 cmd.RunGrafanaCmd()          // pkg/cmd/grafana/main.go\n       \u2514\u2500 MainApp()               // builds *cli.App (github.com/urfave/cli/v2)\n            \u251c\u2500 ServerCommand      // \"grafana server\"\n            \u2514\u2500 CLICommand         // \"grafana cli\"\n```\n\n**Legacy binary** \u2014 `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/main.go`\n\nA thin shim that calls `cmd.RunGrafanaCmd(\"server\")`. It exists for backward compatibility with init scripts that invoke `grafana-server` directly.\n\n### 2.2 Server Lifecycle\n\nThe server is constructed and run in `pkg/server/server.go`:\n\n```\nserver.New(cfg, \u2026)\n  \u2514\u2500 newServer()                  // allocates Server struct\n       \u2514\u2500 s.Init()                // calls Init() on every registered service\n            \u2514\u2500 s.Run()            // starts all BackgroundService goroutines\n                 \u2514\u2500 s.Shutdown()  // graceful drain on SIGTERM/SIGINT\n```\n\nThe `Server` struct holds a slice of `registry.BackgroundService` implementations. Each service's `Run(ctx)` goroutine is started concurrently; the server waits for all of them to exit before returning.\n\n### 2.3 Dependency Injection with Google Wire\n\nAll service wiring lives in `pkg/server/wire.go`. Grafana uses [Google Wire](https://github.com/google/wire) for compile-time dependency injection. The key provider sets are:\n\n| Wire set | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `wireBasicSet` | Minimal set for lightweight commands |\n| `wireSet` | Full production server |\n| `wireCLISet` | CLI-only commands |\n| `wireTestSet` | Integration test overrides |\n\nThe top-level initializers generated by Wire are:\n\n```go\nInitialize()              // production server\nInitializeForTest()       // test server\nInitializeForCLI()        // CLI commands\nInitializeModuleServer()  // modular server mode\nInitializeAPIServerFactory()\n```\n\nWire reads the `ProvideXxx` constructor functions across all packages and generates the wiring code in `wire_gen.go`. When you add a new service, you add its `ProvideXxx` function to the appropriate Wire set in `wire.go`.\n\n### 2.4 HTTP Server\n\n`pkg/api/http_server.go` defines `HTTPServer`, which aggregates every service needed to handle HTTP requests (100+ injected fields). Route registration happens in `pkg/api/api.go` via `registerRoutes()`, which mounts handlers for the REST API, plugin proxy, live streaming, and static assets.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Core Backend Packages\n\n### 3.1 Service Registry \u2014 `pkg/registry`\n\n```go\n// BackgroundService is implemented by any service that needs a long-running goroutine.\ntype BackgroundService interface {\n    Run(ctx context.Context) error\n}\n\n// CanBeDisabled lets a service opt out at runtime based on configuration.\ntype CanBeDisabled interface {\n    IsDisabled() bool\n}\n```\n\nEvery service that needs to run continuously (alerting scheduler, provisioning poller, live streaming, etc.) implements `BackgroundService`. The server collects all of them via Wire and starts them in `s.Run()`.\n\n### 3.2 Configuration \u2014 `pkg/setting`\n\n`setting.Cfg` is the central configuration struct populated from `grafana.ini` (and environment variable overrides). It is injected everywhere via Wire. Key fields include database connection strings, plugin paths, provisioning paths, feature toggles, and security settings.\n\n### 3.3 Infrastructure \u2014 `pkg/infra`\n\n| Sub-package | Responsibility |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/infra/db` | Database abstraction (SQLite / MySQL / PostgreSQL via `xorm`) |\n| `pkg/infra/log` | Structured logger (wraps `go-kit/log`) |\n| `pkg/infra/metrics` | Prometheus metrics registration |\n| `pkg/infra/tracing` | OpenTelemetry tracing |\n| `pkg/infra/kvstore` | Key-value store abstraction |\n\n### 3.4 Domain Services \u2014 `pkg/services`\n\nEach domain area lives in its own package under `pkg/services/`:\n\n| Package | Responsibility |\n|---|---|\n| `authn` | Authentication pipeline \u2014 `authn.go` defines the `Service` interface; `authnimpl/` holds the implementation; `clients/` contains individual auth clients (API key, JWT, LDAP, OAuth, \u2026) |\n| `dashboards` | Dashboard CRUD, `DashboardService` and `DashboardProvisioningService` interfaces |\n| `datasources` | Datasource CRUD, `DataSourceService` interface |\n| `folder` | Folder hierarchy management |\n| `ngalert` | Alerting engine \u2014 scheduler, evaluator, notifier, state machine, provisioning |\n| `accesscontrol` | Role-based access control (RBAC) |\n| `featuremgmt` | Feature toggle evaluation |\n| `quota` | Resource quota enforcement |\n| `secrets` | Secret encryption/decryption |\n| `org` | Multi-org management |\n\n### 3.5 Plugin System \u2014 `pkg/plugins`\n\nThe plugin system is described in detail in [Section 4](#4-datasource-plugin-architecture). The top-level `pkg/plugins/plugins.go` defines the `Plugin` struct and the four plugin types:\n\n```go\nconst (\n    TypeDatasource      Type = \"datasource\"\n    TypePanel           Type = \"panel\"\n    TypeApp             Type = \"app\"\n    TypeRenderer        Type = \"renderer\"\n    TypeSecretsManager  Type = \"secretsmanager\"\n)\n```\n\nAnd four plugin classes:\n\n```go\nconst (\n    ClassCore     Class = \"core\"     // compiled into the binary (pkg/tsdb/*)\n    ClassBundled  Class = \"bundled\"  // shipped with Grafana, loaded from disk\n    ClassExternal Class = \"external\" // installed by users\n    ClassCDN      Class = \"cdn\"      // loaded from Grafana CDN\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Datasource Plugin Architecture\n\nGrafana datasource plugins have two halves: a **backend** (Go) that executes queries and a **frontend** (TypeScript) that renders the query editor. The two halves are linked by a shared plugin ID declared in `plugin.json`.\n\n### 4.1 Plugin Lifecycle Pipeline\n\nPlugin loading is orchestrated through a five-stage pipeline defined in `pkg/services/pluginsintegration/`:\n\n```\nDiscovery  \u2192  Bootstrap  \u2192  Validation  \u2192  Initialization  \u2192  (Termination)\n   \u2193              \u2193              \u2193                \u2193\nfinder.go    bootstrap/     validation/      initialization/\n             pipeline       pipeline         pipeline\n```\n\n1. **Discovery** (`pipeline/discovery`) \u2014 scans configured plugin directories and the CDN for `plugin.json` manifests.\n2. **Bootstrap** (`pipeline/bootstrap`) \u2014 reads and parses each `plugin.json` into a `plugins.Plugin` struct.\n3. **Validation** (`pipeline/validation`) \u2014 verifies plugin signatures; unsigned plugins are rejected in production unless explicitly allowed.\n4. **Initialization** (`pipeline/initialization`) \u2014 starts the backend process (gRPC or in-process) and registers the plugin in the registry.\n5. **Termination** (`pipeline/termination`) \u2014 gracefully stops backend processes on unload.\n\n### 4.2 Core Datasource Backends\n\nCore datasources (Prometheus, Loki, Elasticsearch, etc.) are compiled directly into the Grafana binary. They live in `pkg/tsdb/` and are registered in `pkg/plugins/backendplugin/coreplugin/registry.go`:\n\n```go\n// ProvideCoreRegistry wires every core datasource service into a Registry.\nfunc ProvideCoreRegistry(tracer, am, cw, cm, es, \u2026) *Registry {\n    return NewRegistry(map[string]backendplugin.PluginFactoryFunc{\n        \"cloudwatch\":                      asBackendPlugin(cw.Executor),\n        \"prometheus\":                      asBackendPlugin(pr),\n        \"loki\":                            asBackendPlugin(lk),\n        \"grafana-postgresql-datasource\":   asBackendPlugin(pg),\n        // \u2026 17 total core datasources\n    })\n}\n```\n\n`asBackendPlugin` wraps any service that implements one or more of the SDK handler interfaces (`QueryDataHandler`, `CallResourceHandler`, `CheckHealthHandler`, `StreamHandler`) into a `backendplugin.PluginFactoryFunc`.\n\n### 4.3 External Datasource Backends (gRPC)\n\nExternal datasource plugins run as child processes and communicate over gRPC using [hashicorp/go-plugin](https://github.com/hashicorp/go-plugin). The implementation is in `pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/grpc_plugin.go`:\n\n```\nGrafana process                    Plugin process\n\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500                  \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\ngrpcPlugin.Start()\n  \u2514\u2500 plugin.NewClient()  \u2500\u2500gRPC\u2500\u2500\u25ba plugin binary\n       \u2514\u2500 newClientV2()            implements backend.QueryDataHandler\n                                              backend.CheckHealthHandler\n                                              backend.CallResourceHandler\n                                              backend.StreamHandler\n```\n\nThe `grpcPlugin` struct implements the full `backendplugin.Plugin` interface, delegating every call (`QueryData`, `CheckHealth`, `CallResource`, `SubscribeStream`, `RunStream`, \u2026) to the remote process via `ClientV2`.\n\n### 4.4 Backend SDK Interfaces\n\nAll datasource backends (core and external) implement interfaces from `github.com/grafana/grafana-plugin-sdk-go/backend`:\n\n```go\ntype QueryDataHandler interface {\n    QueryData(ctx context.Context, req *QueryDataRequest) (*QueryDataResponse, error)\n}\ntype CheckHealthHandler interface {\n    CheckHealth(ctx context.Context, req *CheckHealthRequest) (*CheckHealthResult, error)\n}\ntype CallResourceHandler interface {\n    CallResource(ctx context.Context, req *CallResourceRequest, sender CallResourceResponseSender) error\n}\ntype StreamHandler interface {\n    SubscribeStream(ctx context.Context, req *SubscribeStreamRequest) (*SubscribeStreamResponse, error)\n    RunStream(ctx context.Context, req *RunStreamRequest, sender *StreamSender) error\n    PublishStream(ctx context.Context, req *PublishStreamRequest) (*PublishStreamResponse, error)\n}\n```\n\n### 4.5 Datasource Proxy\n\nHTTP requests from the browser to a datasource's own HTTP API are routed through `pkg/services/datasourceproxy/datasourceproxy.go`. The proxy authenticates the request, resolves the datasource URL from the database, and forwards the request \u2014 adding any configured auth headers (Basic, Bearer, etc.).\n\n### 4.6 Frontend Datasource Plugin\n\nEach datasource has a TypeScript module under `public/app/plugins/datasource/<id>/`. The module exports a class extending `DataSourceApi` from `@grafana/data` and a `QueryEditor` React component. The plugin is loaded at runtime via SystemJS.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Dashboard Provisioning Pipeline\n\nProvisioning lets operators manage Grafana resources (dashboards, datasources, plugins, alerting) as code \u2014 YAML files on disk that Grafana reads at startup and polls for changes.\n\n### 5.1 Top-Level Orchestrator\n\n`pkg/services/provisioning/provisioning.go` \u2014 `ProvisioningServiceImpl` \u2014 is a `BackgroundService` that owns all four provisioning domains:\n\n```go\ntype ProvisioningServiceImpl struct {\n    newDashboardProvisioner dashboards.DashboardProvisionerFactory\n    provisionDatasources    func(ctx, path, \u2026) error\n    provisionPlugins        func(ctx, path, \u2026) error\n    provisionAlerting       func(ctx, \u2026) error\n    // \u2026\n}\n```\n\nOn startup, `Run()` calls each domain's `Provision()` function sequentially, then starts background pollers.\n\n### 5.2 Dashboard Provisioning in Detail\n\nThe dashboard provisioning pipeline has four components:\n\n```\nconf/provisioning/dashboards/*.yaml\n         \u2502\n         \u25bc\n  configReader.readConfig()          // pkg/services/provisioning/dashboards/config_reader.go\n         \u2502  parses YAML (v0 or v1 apiVersion)\n         \u2502  produces []*config\n         \u25bc\n  getFileReaders()                   // dashboard.go\n         \u2502  creates one FileReader per provider config\n         \u25bc\n  Provisioner.Provision()            // dashboard.go\n         \u2502  calls reader.walkDisk(ctx) for each FileReader\n         \u2502  calls duplicateValidator.validate()\n         \u25bc\n  FileReader.walkDisk()              // file_reader.go\n         \u2502  walks the configured path recursively\n         \u2502  for each .json file: reads, parses, upserts via DashboardProvisioningService\n         \u25bc\n  DashboardProvisioningService       // pkg/services/dashboards (database layer)\n```\n\n**Polling** \u2014 `Provisioner.PollChanges(ctx)` launches one goroutine per `FileReader`. Each goroutine calls `walkDisk` on the interval specified by `updateIntervalSeconds` in the provider config (default: 10 s).\n\n**Orphan cleanup** \u2014 `CleanUpOrphanedDashboards` deletes database rows for dashboards whose source file no longer exists.\n\n### 5.3 Provider Config Schema (v1)\n\n```yaml\n# conf/provisioning/dashboards/my-provider.yaml\napiVersion: 1\nproviders:\n  - name: my-dashboards          # unique name\n    type: file                   # only \"file\" is supported\n    orgId: 1\n    folder: MyFolder             # target folder in Grafana UI\n    folderUid: \"\"\n    disableDeletion: false       # keep DB rows when file is deleted\n    updateIntervalSeconds: 30\n    allowUiUpdates: false        # prevent UI edits of provisioned dashboards\n    options:\n      path: /var/lib/grafana/dashboards\n      foldersFromFilesStructure: false  # mirror directory structure as folders\n```\n\n### 5.4 Other Provisioning Domains\n\n| Domain | Config path | Package |\n|---|---|---|\n| Datasources | `conf/provisioning/datasources/` | `pkg/services/provisioning/datasources` |\n| Plugins | `conf/provisioning/plugins/` | `pkg/services/provisioning/plugins` |\n| Alerting | `conf/provisioning/alerting/` | `pkg/services/provisioning/alerting` |\n\nEach domain follows the same pattern: a `configReader` parses YAML, a `Provision` function applies the config to the database, and a background goroutine polls for changes.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Frontend Build System\n\n### 6.1 Technology Stack\n\n| Tool | Role |\n|---|---|\n| **Webpack 5** | Module bundler |\n| **esbuild-loader** | TypeScript/TSX transpilation (replaces ts-loader for speed) |\n| **Sass + PostCSS** | CSS preprocessing |\n| **Nx** | Monorepo task orchestration |\n| **Yarn 4 (Berry)** | Package manager with workspaces |\n| **Jest** | Unit testing |\n| **Cypress / Playwright** | End-to-end testing |\n\n### 6.2 Webpack Configuration\n\nThe Webpack config is split across three files in `scripts/webpack/`:\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `webpack.common.js` | Shared config: entry points, output, module resolution, loaders |\n| `webpack.dev.js` | Development: `webpack-dev-server`, source maps, React Fast Refresh |\n| `webpack.prod.js` | Production: esbuild minification, content-hashed filenames, CSS extraction |\n\n**Entry points** (from `webpack.common.js`):\n\n```js\nentry: {\n  app:     './public/app/index.ts',   // main application bundle\n  swagger: './public/swagger/index.tsx',\n}\n```\n\n**Output** \u2014 all bundles land in `public/build/` with content-hashed filenames (`app.[contenthash].js`). Two manifest files are emitted:\n- `webpack-assets-manifest.json` \u2014 includes SRI integrity hashes (used by the Go server to inject `<script>` tags)\n- `manifest.json` \u2014 simpler filename map\n\n**Module resolution** \u2014 `public/` is added to the resolver's `modules` list, enabling bare imports like `import config from 'app/core/config'`.\n\n### 6.3 npm Workspace Packages\n\nThe `packages/` directory contains the published `@grafana/*` npm packages. They are consumed by the main app as `workspace:*` dependencies:\n\n| Package | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `@grafana/data` | Core data types: `DataFrame`, `PanelPlugin`, `DataSourceApi`, field config, transformers |\n| `@grafana/runtime` | Runtime singletons: `BackendSrv`, `DataSourceSrv`, `locationService`, plugin extension hooks |\n| `@grafana/ui` | React component library: `Button`, `Select`, `Table`, `PanelChrome`, etc. |\n| `@grafana/schema` | CUE-generated TypeScript types for panel/datasource schemas |\n| `@grafana/prometheus` | Shared Prometheus query editor components |\n| `@grafana/sql` | Shared SQL query editor components |\n\nBuild all packages: `yarn packages:build` (runs `nx run-many -t build --projects='@grafana/*'`).\n\n### 6.4 Frontend Bootstrap Sequence\n\n```\npublic/app/index.ts\n  \u2514\u2500 public/app/app.ts\n       \u251c\u2500 Registers @grafana/runtime singletons\n       \u2502    (setBackendSrv, setDataSourceSrv, setLocationSrv, \u2026)\n       \u251c\u2500 Initializes i18n (initializeI18n)\n       \u251c\u2500 Registers standard field config editors and transformers\n       \u251c\u2500 Loads icon cache\n       \u2514\u2500 Mounts <AppWrapper /> into #reactRoot via React 18 createRoot()\n```\n\n`AppWrapper.tsx` sets up the Redux store, React Router, and the `GrafanaContext` provider before rendering the main application shell.\n\n### 6.5 Common Development Commands\n\n```bash\n# Start dev server with hot reload\nyarn start\n\n# Production build\nyarn build\n\n# Run unit tests in watch mode\nyarn test\n\n# Type-check everything\nyarn typecheck\n\n# Lint TypeScript\nyarn lint:ts\n\n# Build all @grafana/* packages\nyarn packages:build\n\n# Build all bundled panel plugins\nyarn plugin:build\n```\n\n---\n\n## 7. Adding a New Panel Plugin\n\nPanel plugins are pure frontend \u2014 they require no Go code. A panel plugin consists of a `plugin.json` manifest, a `module.tsx` entry point, and a React component.\n\n### 7.1 File Structure\n\nCreate a new directory under `public/app/plugins/panel/<your-plugin-id>/`:\n\n```\npublic/app/plugins/panel/my-panel/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 plugin.json          # Plugin metadata\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 module.tsx           # Plugin registration (must export `plugin`)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 MyPanel.tsx          # React panel component\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 types.ts             # Options and FieldConfig TypeScript types\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 panelcfg.cue         # (optional) CUE schema for options\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 img/\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 icon.svg         # Panel icon shown in the panel picker\n```\n\n### 7.2 `plugin.json`\n\n```json\n{\n  \"type\": \"panel\",\n  \"name\": \"My Panel\",\n  \"id\": \"my-panel\",\n  \"info\": {\n    \"description\": \"A short description of what this panel does\",\n    \"author\": {\n      \"name\": \"Your Name\",\n      \"url\": \"https://example.com\"\n    },\n    \"logos\": {\n      \"small\": \"img/icon.svg\",\n      \"large\": \"img/icon.svg\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\nThe `id` field must be globally unique. For built-in panels it is a simple slug (e.g., `timeseries`, `table`). For external plugins it is conventionally namespaced (e.g., `myorg-mypanel-panel`).\n\n### 7.3 `module.tsx` \u2014 Plugin Registration\n\nThe file **must** export a named constant `plugin` of type `PanelPlugin`. Grafana's plugin loader looks for this export by convention.\n\n```tsx\nimport { PanelPlugin } from '@grafana/data';\nimport { MyPanel } from './MyPanel';\n\n// Minimal panel \u2014 no options\nexport const plugin = new PanelPlugin<Options>(MyPanel);\n```\n\nA more complete example with options and field config (modelled on the built-in `timeseries` panel at `public/app/plugins/panel/timeseries/module.tsx`):\n\n```tsx\nimport { PanelPlugin } from '@grafana/data';\nimport { MyPanel } from './MyPanel';\nimport { Options, FieldConfig } from './types';\n\nexport const plugin = new PanelPlugin<Options, FieldConfig>(MyPanel)\n  // Declare panel-level options (shown in the panel editor sidebar)\n  .setPanelOptions((builder) => {\n    builder\n      .addBooleanSwitch({\n        path: 'showLegend',\n        name: 'Show legend',\n        defaultValue: true,\n      })\n      .addSelect({\n        path: 'colorMode',\n        name: 'Color mode',\n        defaultValue: 'palette',\n        settings: {\n          options: [\n            { value: 'palette', label: 'Palette' },\n            { value: 'fixed', label: 'Fixed color' },\n          ],\n        },\n      });\n  })\n  // Declare per-field overrides (shown in the Overrides tab)\n  .useFieldConfig({\n    standardOptions: {\n      color: { fixedColorMode: 'fixed' },\n    },\n    useCustomConfig: (builder) => {\n      builder.addNumberInput({\n        path: 'lineWidth',\n        name: 'Line width',\n        defaultValue: 1,\n      });\n    },\n  })\n  // Handle migration from a previous panel type\n  .setPanelChangeHandler((panel, prevPluginId, prevOptions) => {\n    if (prevPluginId === 'graph') {\n      return { ...panel, options: { showLegend: true } };\n    }\n    return panel;\n  })\n  // Declare what data features the panel supports\n  .setDataSupport({ annotations: false, alertStates: false });\n```\n\n### 7.4 `MyPanel.tsx` \u2014 The React Component\n\n```tsx\nimport React from 'react';\nimport { PanelProps } from '@grafana/data';\nimport { Options } from './types';\n\n// PanelProps<Options> provides: data, options, width, height, timeRange,\n// timeZone, onOptionsChange, onFieldConfigChange, replaceVariables, \u2026\nexport function MyPanel({ data, options, width, height }: PanelProps<Options>) {\n  const frame = data.series[0];\n\n  if (!frame) {\n    return <div>No data</div>;\n  }\n\n  return (\n    <div style={{ width, height, overflow: 'auto' }}>\n      {options.showLegend && <div className=\"legend\">Legend</div>}\n      {/* render your visualization here */}\n    </div>\n  );\n}\n```\n\n### 7.5 `types.ts` \u2014 Options and FieldConfig\n\n```ts\n// Panel-level options (one set per panel instance)\nexport interface Options {\n  showLegend: boolean;\n  colorMode: 'palette' | 'fixed';\n}\n\n// Per-field config (can be overridden per series/field)\nexport interface FieldConfig {\n  lineWidth?: number;\n}\n```\n\n### 7.6 Registering the Plugin with the Build System\n\nBuilt-in panel plugins are automatically discovered by Webpack because `public/app/plugins/panel/` is included in the Yarn workspace glob:\n\n```json\n// package.json (root)\n\"workspaces\": {\n  \"packages\": [\n    \"public/app/plugins/*/*\"   // \u2190 picks up your new panel\n  ]\n}\n```\n\nNo additional registration step is needed for built-in panels. The plugin loader resolves `module.tsx` at runtime via SystemJS using the plugin ID from `plugin.json`.\n\nFor **external** plugins (distributed separately), you would instead use the `@grafana/create-plugin` scaffolding tool and the `@grafana/plugin-configs` Webpack preset from `packages/grafana-plugin-configs/`.\n\n### 7.7 Testing Your Panel\n\n```bash\n# Unit tests \u2014 create MyPanel.test.tsx alongside MyPanel.tsx\nyarn test --testPathPattern=my-panel\n\n# Start the dev server and open Grafana at http://localhost:3000\n# Add a new panel to a dashboard and select \"My Panel\" from the panel picker\nyarn start\n```\n\n### 7.8 Key `PanelPlugin` Builder Methods Reference\n\n| Method | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `setPanelOptions(builder => \u2026)` | Declare panel-level option editors |\n| `useFieldConfig({ standardOptions, useCustomConfig })` | Declare per-field config editors |\n| `setPanelChangeHandler(fn)` | Migrate options when switching from another panel type |\n| `setDataSupport({ annotations, alertStates })` | Opt in to annotations/alert state overlays |\n| `setSuggestionsSupplier(supplier)` | Provide auto-suggestions in the panel picker |\n| `setNoPadding()` | Remove the default panel padding (useful for map/canvas panels) |\n| `setSkipDataQuery()` | Panel does not query data (e.g., text, image panels) |\n\n---\n\n## Quick Reference: Key Files\n\n| What you want to understand | File(s) to read |\n|---|---|\n| How the server starts | `pkg/cmd/grafana/main.go`, `pkg/server/server.go` |\n| How services are wired together | `pkg/server/wire.go` |\n| How HTTP routes are registered | `pkg/api/api.go`, `pkg/api/http_server.go` |\n| How to add a background service | `pkg/registry/registry.go` (implement `BackgroundService`) |\n| How core datasources are registered | `pkg/plugins/backendplugin/coreplugin/registry.go` |\n| How external plugins communicate | `pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/grpc_plugin.go` |\n| How panel plugin is structured | `public/app/plugins/panel/timeseries/module.tsx` |\n| Webpack entry points and output | `scripts/webpack/webpack.common.js` |\n| Published npm packages | `packages/`
